  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0b2a1c14-1c21-44ae-9005-0c884702b589'
      });
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer14748645211443418123">Der siebzehnjährige Phil ist auf der Suche. So wenig er über seine Vergangenheit weiß, so chaotisch ist seine Gegenwart. Da ist zum Beispiel seine Mutter Glass mit ihren ständig wechselnden Liebhabern. Oder seine Zwillingsschwester Dianne, schroff und eigenwillig, mit Geheimnissen, die sie längst nicht mehr mit Phil teilt. Oder Annie, die verrückte Alte mit den roten Schuh</span>
  <span id="freeText14748645211443418123" style="display:none">Der siebzehnjährige Phil ist auf der Suche. So wenig er über seine Vergangenheit weiß, so chaotisch ist seine Gegenwart. Da ist zum Beispiel seine Mutter Glass mit ihren ständig wechselnden Liebhabern. Oder seine Zwillingsschwester Dianne, schroff und eigenwillig, mit Geheimnissen, die sie längst nicht mehr mit Phil teilt. Oder Annie, die verrückte Alte mit den roten Schuhen, die sich ausschließlich von Kirschlikör zu ernähren scheint und Nicholas, der Unerreichbare, in den sich Phil unsterblich verliebt hat. Phil sehnt sich nach Orientierung und Perspektiven. Und vor allem danach, mehr über sich selbst zu erfahren ...</span>

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">Eine weniger poetische Antwort ist, dass es in einer Kleinstadt in Deutschland spielt. Es gibt kleine Hinweise im Buch, die dabei helfen, den Ort noch<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Eine weniger poetische Antwort ist, dass es in einer Kleinstadt in Deutschland spielt. Es gibt kleine Hinweise im Buch, die dabei helfen, den Ort noch etwas besser zu beschreiben, aber eine wirklich genaue Angabe gibt es nicht.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

<div id="review_1244606225" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1244606225" />
    <a title="Kai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41788524-kai"><img alt="Kai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573562141p2/41788524.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1244606225?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842705865" href="/book/show/1382534.The_Centre_of_My_World">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Markus Zusak, Adam Silvera, Benjamin Alire Saénz Shaun David Hutchinson</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=underrated">underrated</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=queer">queer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=read-for-uni">read-for-uni</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1244606225" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5833621436130135510"><i>"This was the reason I loved the library. For me it was the centre of the world."</i><br/><br/><i>The Centre of My World</i> is a wondrous and touching tale of childhood and adolescence, that reminded me of <i>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</i>. But better. Fight me.<br/><br/><b>Update:</b><br/>I loved this book even more the second time around. The frustration that I felt when I read <i>The Centre of My World</i> for the first time was gone. Two years ago, the pacing was much too slow for my taste. Childhood flashbacks kept </span>
  <span id="freeText5833621436130135510" style="display:none"><i>"This was the reason I loved the library. For me it was the centre of the world."</i><br /><br /><i>The Centre of My World</i> is a wondrous and touching tale of childhood and adolescence, that reminded me of <i>Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe</i>. But better. Fight me.<br /><br /><b>Update:</b><br />I loved this book even more the second time around. The frustration that I felt when I read <i>The Centre of My World</i> for the first time was gone. Two years ago, the pacing was much too slow for my taste. Childhood flashbacks kept interrupting the main plot and drove me nuts. The romance was less romantic than I had wanted it to be. The ending was...not enough. Rereading it helped because I could take my mind off what was being told and instead focus on how it was told. That's also the reason why I added a star to my rating.<br />You can also watch the film adaption of this book which is totally worth watching because the main actors are very nice to look at (and so are their butts). This is one of the few German books that I am really proud of. It was written more than 20 years ago but it feels timeless. There aren't many great LGBT books in the German YA category, and even less OwnVoices books (aka gay books written by an actual gay author). <i>The Centre of My World</i> is a rare gemstone and you shouldn't deprive yourself of this experience.<br /><br /><b>Original review:</b><br /><br />Phil lives in an old and crumbling mansion named Visible, together with his twin sister Dianne and their mother Glass. They make for a rather unusual family. Glass despises being called "Mom" and refuses to enter into a lasting relationship with any of the long list of men that go in and out of Visible. Phil wishes for nothing more than someone he can call "Dad", and still, he doesn't even know his father's name. Dianne has a deep understanding of everything that flutters and crawls through their garden, and people whisper that she can talk to animals. No wonder the town folk warn their children to stay far away from these people. Phil and Dianne don't mind their unusual lifestyle. That is, not until they grow up and stop talking to each other, for a reason Phil doesn't understand. And then again, there's Nicholas, the new guy in Phil's year, and he may make things even more confusing.<br /><br />What makes <i>The Centre of My World</i> so remarkable is its outstanding prose and its fragile but headstrong characters. The writing is vibrant and nostalgic. Andreas Steinhöfel captures the feeling of youth, awkward discoveries of growing up and bittersweet memories perfectly. Phil is so relatable because he impersonates all of those feelings that come with first crushes, love, friendship and family.<br />Here is one of my favourite passages from the book:<br /><br /><i>"Imagine life as a huge house with lots of rooms, Phil. Some of these rooms are empty, and others are full of junk. Some are big and filled with light, and others are dark and hide terror and grief. And from time to time - but only from time to time, mind you - the door to one of these scary rooms opens and you have to look inside whether you want to or not. That makes you terribly frightened, like now. So you know what you do then?"<br />I shook my head.<br />"Then you imagine it's your life - your house, with your rooms. You have the keys, Phil. So you just shut the door of that scary room."<br />"And I throw the key away!"<br />"No, you mustn't do that, ever," replied Tereza. "Because one day you may realize that this scary room is the only way you can reach a bigger, more beautiful part of the house. And then you'll need the key. You can lock out your fear for a while, but at some point you have to face up to it."</i><br /><br />That, my fellow readers, was Andreas Steinhöfel spitting mental health advice since 1998. Now, I must admit that the translation doesn't do the German original complete justice, but the message is the same one.<br /><br />Personally, I would have wished for fewer flashbacks and a thicker plot instead. The ending didn't satisfy me completely. There was too much left unsaid for my taste. But then again nothing in life is certain. Luckily there is a collection of short stories, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/827083.Defender_Geschichten_aus_der_Mitte_der_Welt" title="Defender Geschichten aus der Mitte der Welt by Andreas Steinhöfel" rel="nofollow noopener">Defender : Geschichten aus der Mitte der Welt</a>, that may answer some questions (update: no it doesn't. You'll only have more questions).<br /><br /><i>The Centre of My World</i> is one underrated novel. If you're looking for a new(ish) voice in LGBT books, a coming of age tale, a portrayal of strong and independent women, or just a good book to dive into, this is perfect for you.<br /><br />Life is ironic, funny, raw, sad and beautiful. So is this novel.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="5833621436130135510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_63923323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Tamer Lorika" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2470907-tamer-lorika"><img alt="Tamer Lorika" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1246382714p2/2470907.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63923323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17230020217805556048">You know what? I didn't love it. I didn't even like it. I hated the constant flashbacks, I hated waiting in fear for what was going to happen in the REAL story, and then having the whole premise of "before the flashback" completely forgotten. But at the same time, this book HAS to be read. There is something so ... true. So undervalued and true about this book. This is real. This is life. The author just reflects a life in progress in a way that completely and perfectly details everyone else's l</span>
  <span id="freeText17230020217805556048" style="display:none">You know what? I didn't love it. I didn't even like it. I hated the constant flashbacks, I hated waiting in fear for what was going to happen in the REAL story, and then having the whole premise of "before the flashback" completely forgotten. But at the same time, this book HAS to be read. There is something so ... true. So undervalued and true about this book. This is real. This is life. The author just reflects a life in progress in a way that completely and perfectly details everyone else's life in progress in a way I don't understand. And every moment, I can't find a reason to hate the protagonist. None at all. Even though he's stupid and naiive and petty, he's ME. He's YOU. He's EVERYONE. <br /><br />This book isn't what I wanted. I never wanted it to end like this. "I never asked for this". But its the way it IS, and everyone has to read it, to know.</span>

<div id="review_412135838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/412135838" />
    <a title="Ellinor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8307014-ellinor"><img alt="Ellinor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1573658130p2/8307014.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/412135838?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ellinor" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ellinor" href="/user/show/8307014-ellinor">Ellinor</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783866151253" href="/book/show/1473572.Die_Mitte_der_Welt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8307014-ellinor?shelf=sz-junge-bibliothek">sz-junge-bibliothek</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8307014-ellinor?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer412135838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6530083822579563254">This is by far the best YA novel on homosexuality I have read so far. While <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson' title='Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green' rel='nofollow noopener'>Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a> is the loud version of this topic, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1610138.The_Center_of_the_World' title='The Center of the World by Andreas Steinhöfel' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Center of the World</a> is the quiet version - and in my opinion also the better one. I'm usually not much touched by homosexual relationships but here I felt with Phil so much.<br/>The story makes slow progress: the actual story is frequently interrupted by flashbacks to past occurrences that have an influence on what is happening later. Secrets from the past are </span>
  <span id="freeText6530083822579563254" style="display:none">This is by far the best YA novel on homosexuality I have read so far. While <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6567017.Will_Grayson__Will_Grayson" title="Will Grayson, Will Grayson by John Green" rel="nofollow noopener">Will Grayson, Will Grayson</a> is the loud version of this topic, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1610138.The_Center_of_the_World" title="The Center of the World by Andreas Steinhöfel" rel="nofollow noopener">The Center of the World</a> is the quiet version - and in my opinion also the better one. I'm usually not much touched by homosexual relationships but here I felt with Phil so much.<br />The story makes slow progress: the actual story is frequently interrupted by flashbacks to past occurrences that have an influence on what is happening later. Secrets from the past are only revealred step by step and this way tension is built up. The special setting - a giant old house outside a fictional town - further contributes to this. <br />The language is very poetic and never flashy. This is something which always makes me immensely enjoy a novel. Here, it is also one of the main reasons for my 5-star-rating: the story itself made for a very solid 4 or maybe 4.5 rating. But I loved the language and the way the book deals with homosexuality so much that I just had to give 5 stars. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6530083822579563254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1407756777989931835">I was hooked to this story from the first page. The writing style is bold, yet detailed. It's extremely deep too. <br/>This story is about 17-year-old Phil, who is a misfit in his own town due to his mother's bad reputation. Right at the beginning of the book we are pulled into a strange and mysterious world, full of the ghosts of Phil's past. His only friend is Kat, who shares her boy troubles with him while he mopes about his non-existent ones. Phil's family has never been close; his mother, Glass,</span>
  <span id="freeText1407756777989931835" style="display:none">I was hooked to this story from the first page. The writing style is bold, yet detailed. It's extremely deep too. <br />This story is about 17-year-old Phil, who is a misfit in his own town due to his mother's bad reputation. Right at the beginning of the book we are pulled into a strange and mysterious world, full of the ghosts of Phil's past. His only friend is Kat, who shares her boy troubles with him while he mopes about his non-existent ones. Phil's family has never been close; his mother, Glass, is known to have slept around with numerous men, and the only thing Phil knows about his father is that he was number 3. on Glass's long list of flings. Phil's sister is becoming more secretive and is shutting Phil out of her life. But things change for Phil when the handsome and mysterious newcomer Nicholas comes into Phil's world. <br />I really have to say that this is a very.... mature novel, not the usual kind of young adult book. The family dynamics is told amazingly, with each of the characters having their own "baggage" so to say. Just read it and be dragged down into the depth of Phil's world..... </span>

<div id="review_281381072" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/281381072" />
    <a title="Nessi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7262723-nessi"><img alt="Nessi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451319857p2/7262723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/281381072?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nessi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nessi" href="/user/show/7262723-nessi">Nessi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9783551311016" href="/book/show/11973458-die-mitte-der-welt">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7262723-nessi?shelf=mm">mm</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer281381072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7209807754255979655">Warning: Spoilers!!<br/><br/>honestly? i picked this book up only because of the fact that the main characters name is Phil (i love that name) and 'cause he is gay and gets together with a guy called Nicholas (another name i love since CON) but thats not the reason i actually finished such a thick book in three days.<br/><br/>normally i am not interested in these kinda fictions but i found myself liking it. even the parts which werent about the love relationship. the mystery behind his sister and his mother, the we</span>
  <span id="freeText7209807754255979655" style="display:none">Warning: Spoilers!!<br /><br />honestly? i picked this book up only because of the fact that the main characters name is Phil (i love that name) and 'cause he is gay and gets together with a guy called Nicholas (another name i love since CON) but thats not the reason i actually finished such a thick book in three days.<br /><br />normally i am not interested in these kinda fictions but i found myself liking it. even the parts which werent about the love relationship. the mystery behind his sister and his mother, the weird doll he's been treasuring since he was a child, his first boyfriend (not boyfriend but a friend who is a boy) ever called Wolf and the super jealous guy Thomas who couldnt get over Kat (Phils best friend) leaving him. I found all of these aspects very interesting and wanted to know what was behind it and until a certain point i really really loved the book lots... until Nicholas and Kat slept with each other and did the worst thing ever they could to Phil.<br /><br />Really, i am a quite sensible person and its nothing special for me to cry, be happy or get mad over a book but THIS was just the worst shit ever. the weird thing about it was that i KNEW that this was going to happen the whole time but i just pretended not to see the thing going on between Kat and Nicholas and ignored it. I mean how could an author ever hurt his main character like that? I thought it wouldnt be possible but it was! Andreas did it! He killed Phil and me inside!<br /><br />At this point i started to hate Nicholas. Its not that i really liked him from the beginning since he was kinda weird but somehow even thought he didnt kiss Phil often and didnt tell him that he loved him i thought he did. especially because he had his snow globe the whole time like some kinda symbol that Phil and Nicholas were fated to be together or something. It just hurt so much to see Phil suffer over Nick... i couldnt take it at all but then something happened, that made it all good for me again. Not for Phil but at this point I somehow forgave Andreas for hurting Phil like that. <br />Wolf, Phils first male friend ever, who couldnt ever forget about Phil, hurt Nicholas just as bad as he had hurt Phil. He destroyed one of his eyes O_O thats only fair, isnt it? I mean Nicholas was the worst asshole ever and he just didnt deserve any better... maybe worse but not better so thank you Wolf. You saved that story for me.<br /><br />Actually i think Wolf was somehow in love with Phil. I mean it was never said but the scene when Phil kissed Thomas and Wolf saw everything and touched Phils cheek in such a gentle way... somehow i had the feeling that he love him and that he had always been watching him. Okay guys, Wolf was definitely nuts but even crazy people can have feelings. Oh and the fact that Wolf hurt Nicholas who was so close to Phil... another proof that Phil was still important to him. I think Wolf did it because he didnt want Phil to have such eyes for anyone else... that was also the reason he killed those baby bird... 'cause Phil was so thrilled about them.<br /><br />Hm anyway. At that point i was pretty pleased with the plot again... now only Kat was left to hurt! Only Kat!!! And since Phil is such a disgusting nice guy i was afraid that he would forgive her because of their 12 years of friendship or something but i am happy he didnt. Well, they never talked about it since Phil pretended he didnt know in front of her but Kat wouldnt ever have a chance to apologize or explain it to him or something since Phil made the right decision to leave that place with his uncle Gable. Of course Phil said himself that he is gonna come back, since this was his home but even then i am sure he wouldnt forgive Kat for what she did. With his going away without telling her at all, he officially ended their friendship and that was definitely a good choice.<br /><br />All in all, the book was really nice and realistic. Actually what Nicholas and Kat did is the worst thing i could ever imagine happening to me so seeing that there is a way to get over it made me feel kinda happy. There were many ups and downs in this book but i still liked it a lot. I am pretty sure that i will never ever touch this book again since it made me wanna burn it at some point but when I closed it i did it was a smile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7209807754255979655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2598423477" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2598423477" />
    <a title="Ricardo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6016191-ricardo"><img alt="Ricardo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1537397408p2/6016191.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2598423477?book_show_action=true">Nov 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ricardo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ricardo" href="/user/show/6016191-ricardo">Ricardo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385729437" href="/book/show/1610138.The_Center_of_the_World">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2598423477" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6085441698591787401">This is one of those books that was so different from the movie but at the same time, it was as excellent as the movie itself. I could see all the creative licenses taken in the movie and was glad for the superb casting because otherwise, the movie would have been simply average. This book is such a subtle and simple coming of age story but surrounded in a layer of subplots (the mother’s behaviour, the sister’s, Phil’s interactions with his classmates, his godmother and her girlfriend, etc.). Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6085441698591787401" style="display:none">This is one of those books that was so different from the movie but at the same time, it was as excellent as the movie itself. I could see all the creative licenses taken in the movie and was glad for the superb casting because otherwise, the movie would have been simply average. This book is such a subtle and simple coming of age story but surrounded in a layer of subplots (the mother’s behaviour, the sister’s, Phil’s interactions with his classmates, his godmother and her girlfriend, etc.). There is humor, there is heartache, laughter and tears, and above all, the author manages to write about deeply serious human situations without losing the innocence of a child, always open to new ideas and with the courage to face new things. I love how when Phil decides to go to America, nobody says “you can’t, you’re only 17” or “it’s dangerous, you can’t.” The way they treat him like an adult is the best education I can think of for a teenager, allowing him to find his own way. Wonderful book</span>
  <a data-text-id="6085441698591787401" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_13800068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Gundula" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/808259-gundula"><img alt="Gundula" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1201618140p2/808259.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/13800068?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gundula" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gundula" href="/user/show/808259-gundula">Gundula</a>
      </span>

          added it


          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780440229322" href="/book/show/1382525.The_Center_of_the_World">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer13800068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8051191135999600043">If you never had a chance to dive into a story of surreal family structures - here you go...<br/><br/>Andreas Steinhöfel's The Center of the World tells the story of seventeen-year-old Phil, who lives with his twin sister, Dianne, and mother, Glass, in an old castle in a small German town. The father he has never met and knows little to nothing about remains in America. Glass' promiscuous sexual behavior makes the children targets of the neighborhood bullies' taunts and jeers and relegates them to the rol</span>
  <span id="freeText8051191135999600043" style="display:none">If you never had a chance to dive into a story of surreal family structures - here you go...<br /><br />Andreas Steinhöfel's The Center of the World tells the story of seventeen-year-old Phil, who lives with his twin sister, Dianne, and mother, Glass, in an old castle in a small German town. The father he has never met and knows little to nothing about remains in America. Glass' promiscuous sexual behavior makes the children targets of the neighborhood bullies' taunts and jeers and relegates them to the role of outsiders in the community. Phil is befriended by Kat, the daughter of the school headmaster, who is willful, proud, and possessive. When Phil falls in love with the new boy, Nicholas, Kat supports the relationship but soon finds herself falling for Nicholas' charms, too. In order to nurse and ultimately heal the wounds that result from the love triangle, Phil must decide what is most important to him, accept his own self-worth, and become a more active participant in his life. This novel is rich and multi-layered with several interwoven stories that take the reader backward and forward in time, weaving a complex story of love, betrayal, and family connection. As Phil reveals and reflects upon his relationships with those around him-his sister, his mother, his seafaring uncle, his adult friends, his lover, his enemies, even his absent father-we are pushed and pulled through time and given the opportunity to bear witness to his coming of age.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8051191135999600043" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_284506311" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/284506311" />
    <a title="Andune" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4656897-andune"><img alt="Andune" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1293762258p2/4656897.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/284506311?book_show_action=true">Feb 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andune" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andune" href="/user/show/4656897-andune">Andune</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385729437" href="/book/show/1610138.The_Center_of_the_World">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4656897-andune?shelf=awesomely-favorite-literature">awesomely-favorite-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer284506311" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10446655729356843976">Phil is a young boy who slowly comes to grips with the world around him. He is also an outstanding character in a well thought out novel that speaks about life, love, loss, betrayal and truth. Phil grows up with his twin sister in an old architectural mystery of a home called Visible. His mother is a mix of strength, confusion, independence and hope, who teaches her children not to care about what the Little People on the other side of town think of them. And for the most part, people think they</span>
  <span id="freeText10446655729356843976" style="display:none">Phil is a young boy who slowly comes to grips with the world around him. He is also an outstanding character in a well thought out novel that speaks about life, love, loss, betrayal and truth. Phil grows up with his twin sister in an old architectural mystery of a home called Visible. His mother is a mix of strength, confusion, independence and hope, who teaches her children not to care about what the Little People on the other side of town think of them. And for the most part, people think they are witches and stay well away.<br /><br />I was pulled into this story by not only the quality of the prose, but by all the little quirks and individualisms that made the characters seem very humane. For example, I really loved Phil’s strange weird doll, Paleiko, who speaks very seriously to him and gives him counsel and guidance. I though that was brilliant!<br /><br />The people in this novel are not perfect, in fact sometimes you wonder what is going on in their heads for they can seem mysterious and even cruel, but in reality they are just humans with motivations that aren’t always altruistic, even though they try to do the best they can with what they have. The story doesn’t end in a cliché, is isn’t happily ever after or unhappily ever after. It just is whats it is, a portrayal of the victories and struggles that we all go through and that in the end, hopefully, allow us to discover a bit more of ourselves. I most definitely recommend this novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10446655729356843976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer773439127970634868">This was a wonderful book. I enjoyed the characters, the setting (and especially <i>Visible</i>, I kind of want to live there now), the story and the writing style.<br/>Bo recommended it to me because it's about a gay boy without really being about him being gay, it's not a coming-out story, which I've gotten really tired of.   <span id="freeText773439127970634868" style="display:none">This was a wonderful book. I enjoyed the characters, the setting (and especially <i>Visible</i>, I kind of want to live there now), the story and the writing style.<br />Bo recommended it to me because it's about a gay boy without really being about him being gay, it's not a coming-out story, which I've gotten really tired of. This book is so wonderful because it could be about anyone, Phil's being gay is only a small aspect of it, and he was a nice character even aside from being gay. Y'know, the way I like my characters most.<br />I felt all the feelings that needed to be felt, I got through this book incredibly fast because it's engaging and fast even when it isn't particularly action-packed, interesting, and subtly and quietly beautiful.<br /><br />I'm a bit sad we didn't get to see more Kat near the end, because I needed that kind of closure even if Phil didn't (yet), but other than that there aren't any things that were negative about this book to me.<br /><br />It's enormously recommended for anyone that wants a nice coming-of-age story and a book that deals mostly with family, friendship, love, secrets and life.</span>

<div id="review_1980308085" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Noora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65811666-noora"><img alt="Noora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1550662626p2/65811666.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1252002348" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2983488300565577889">I liked this book even more than the first time I read it about 2 years ago!<br/><br/>In the beginning, it seemed a bit boring and cheesy because of the protagonist's passivity and the many metaphors, but it gets better, especially in the end. The description of the house "Visible" and the nature, combined with a lot of figurative language, creates a mythical atmosphere. Phil's and Dianne's childhood is hard - due to their mother's bad reputation they have the status of outsiders and "Witch-children" - bu</span>
  <span id="freeText2983488300565577889" style="display:none">I liked this book even more than the first time I read it about 2 years ago!<br /><br />In the beginning, it seemed a bit boring and cheesy because of the protagonist's passivity and the many metaphors, but it gets better, especially in the end. The description of the house "Visible" and the nature, combined with a lot of figurative language, creates a mythical atmosphere. Phil's and Dianne's childhood is hard - due to their mother's bad reputation they have the status of outsiders and "Witch-children" - but it seems to be just like a fairytale; with the "castle" they live in, the "enemies" from the other side of the river they fight in an adventurous battle and the strange people they meet on their way, they create a world of their own, in which they are the heroes. <br /><br />Some characters are pretty cliché first and a lot of secrets surround them - especially Dianne, who isolates herself more and more from her family as she grows older - but they become more rounder throughout the book, and some of these weird secrets are even solved, which gives the book a satisfying end.<br /><br />While reading, the many flashbacks distract from the actual storyline and the events are easily mixed up in their chronological order. However, they help to understand the characters better.<br /><br />What I really liked about this book is the big development the characters go through. Phil experiences a lot of pain, learns and fails, and even with the end of the book, his story seems to have only just begun. It is an open ending, and in some points not a good one, but it is full of hope.<br /><br />All in all, this book is a beautiful, quiet story, that may not only be suitable to read by adolescents.<br /><br />UPDATE!: The more I'm thinking about this book and analysing the relationships (especially the twins, since they are the main focus of my term paper) the more I love it! (maybe becuase of the many parallels with greek mythology, which I love?? Idk) tending more and more to 5 stars!</span>
  <a data-text-id="2983488300565577889" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/442666087?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Zenia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Zenia" href="/user/show/7946575-zenia">Zenia</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer442666087" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7388909548847395261">Initially, this was gonna get 3 stars. And I wasn't even going to finish the book.<br/>But I didn't give up and charged through till the end. <br/><br/>I realised that this is a kind of story that you need to be patient with. You need to really understand that even though it is not exciting and not many things are happening, it is still very important. <br/>This book is about loving, loosing, giving, taking, finding out who you are and finding your place in the world. It is about family, friends, trust and betrayal</span>
  <span id="freeText7388909548847395261" style="display:none">Initially, this was gonna get 3 stars. And I wasn't even going to finish the book.<br />But I didn't give up and charged through till the end. <br /><br />I realised that this is a kind of story that you need to be patient with. You need to really understand that even though it is not exciting and not many things are happening, it is still very important. <br />This book is about loving, loosing, giving, taking, finding out who you are and finding your place in the world. It is about family, friends, trust and betrayal. About what it right and wrong, and who decides those things. <br /><br />Phil, Dianne and Glass. A strange little family, not in terms of the world. But in terms of "Those Out There" - what Glass calls the people from the town that her family lives near. <br />These three are so different but also so similar. At times you wouldn't think they are a family, but at other times, like when they are judged by "Those Out There", you can really tell how close they are and how much they have been through together. <br /><br />There are lots and lots of little characters throughout the story, which in a way are all main characters. They each have a history and a little story that comes with it. Some of which I couldn't figure out the point of. But that is probably just me. <br /><br />This book is not for everyone. If you are willing to be patient and understanding, then give it a go. But I cannot guarantee that you will like it. I hope you like it, and hope you understand it. Because in the end this is a very beautiful and deep story. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7388909548847395261" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781299009561" href="/book/show/18410469-the-center-of-the-world">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26880712-alex-luceli-jim-nez?shelf=cr%C3%A8me-de-la-cr%C3%A8me">crème-de-la-crème</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer898999643" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2769249868700827993">It doesn't quite suffice to say that THE CENTER OF THE WORLD is my favourite book; I'd like to say something more powerful. However, it is my favourite book and that is the simplest way to put it. <br/><br/>It's a coming of age novel, really, and the main character is gay. But his sexuality isn't the main focus of the book, and that normalises homosexuality. One can be gay and not have ot be the main focus of their life. When I read this book, I was having the customary sexuality crisis. This book played </span>
  <span id="freeText2769249868700827993" style="display:none">It doesn't quite suffice to say that THE CENTER OF THE WORLD is my favourite book; I'd like to say something more powerful. However, it is my favourite book and that is the simplest way to put it. <br /><br />It's a coming of age novel, really, and the main character is gay. But his sexuality isn't the main focus of the book, and that normalises homosexuality. One can be gay and not have ot be the main focus of their life. When I read this book, I was having the customary sexuality crisis. This book played a major part in helping me accepting my own nature. <br /><br />The writing is beautiful. Steinhöfel is a master with words. The prose seems more like poetry, and it repeatedly whisks you away. This novel easily entrances you, takes you away to some magical area of Germany, and makes you feel everything that Phil, Diana, Glass feels. There's the main story, and then there is intervals when moments when Phil recounts past experiences -- all very profound happenings that shaped him into who he is today. <br /><br />This is most definitely a read that I recommend. <br /><br />I can only hope that the sequel of sorts is translated into English soon. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2769249868700827993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643451458?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dana Petrovski" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dana Petrovski" href="/user/show/39115335-dana-petrovski">Dana Petrovski</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9786176792246" href="/book/show/28761997">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643451458" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8383274923589940362">I've rather enjoyed this book, aside from some minor issues. The development of the plot is a bit uneven, slow paced in the first half and too eventful near the end. But the characters are very lifelike, both lovable and irritating, their motivation and behavior understandable and realistic even when very silly. The atmosphere built by author is perfect, it's easy to imagine yourself in Visible and nearby town, everything is very vivid. The constellation of incidental characters is another littl</span>
  <span id="freeText8383274923589940362" style="display:none">I've rather enjoyed this book, aside from some minor issues. The development of the plot is a bit uneven, slow paced in the first half and too eventful near the end. But the characters are very lifelike, both lovable and irritating, their motivation and behavior understandable and realistic even when very silly. The atmosphere built by author is perfect, it's easy to imagine yourself in Visible and nearby town, everything is very vivid. The constellation of incidental characters is another little charming gem of the book.<br /><br />The ending would be not for everybody's taste. It is not happy, it is not tragic, and it feels a bit like deus ex machin twist of the plot, which I didn't like. But overall impression from the book is good, and I readily recommend it for anyone who like deep and thoughtful coming-of-age books about young adults who have problems connecting with other people (and what young adult have not, eh?).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8383274923589940362" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2278282879" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2278282879" />
    <a title="Shinia Lambert" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4093079-shinia-lambert"><img alt="Shinia Lambert" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524514131p2/4093079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2278282879?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shinia Lambert" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shinia Lambert" href="/user/show/4093079-shinia-lambert">Shinia Lambert</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781842705865" href="/book/show/1382534.The_Centre_of_My_World">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2278282879" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer474724673361776503">This book is so much more than just a tale about a teenage boy trying to come to grips with his sexuality--to believe or conclude as much is a total disservice to both the characters and the reader. If you enjoy a fast paced plot and pages of dialogue--this book isn't for you. But if you enjoy getting to know a character--so intimately that when the book is over, you wonder when you'll see him again, then welcome to Visible, the large looming house on the hill. <br/><br/>Phil is a seventeen year old boy, </span>
  <span id="freeText474724673361776503" style="display:none">This book is so much more than just a tale about a teenage boy trying to come to grips with his sexuality--to believe or conclude as much is a total disservice to both the characters and the reader. If you enjoy a fast paced plot and pages of dialogue--this book isn't for you. But if you enjoy getting to know a character--so intimately that when the book is over, you wonder when you'll see him again, then welcome to Visible, the large looming house on the hill. <br /><br />Phil is a seventeen year old boy, twin to a moody, often disconnected twin, Dianne; and son of Glass--the town's favorite woman to hate. Phil doesn't question his sexuality--he's quite confident of the fact that he is gay. What Phil does question is whether he'll ever have an opportunity to love--and if he does, will he even know how? <br /><br />He's grown distant from his sister; never truly understood his mother (though he loves her fiercely); never knew his father and isn't sure whether his best friend Kat would remain his friend if she didn't have a way to benefit from it. <br /><br />In the pages of this book Phil reflects on events from his past and like pieces of a puzzle beautifully coming together, the reader hears firsthand from Phil each memory that has shaped the young man he's become. And the reader can't help but wonder if Phil is finally coming to grips with his past as well--almost as if he's recalling these events to mind for the very first time. This book makes you reflect on how your own story was written, and all the different people, places, and events that wrote on the slate of who you have become. <br /><br />The Centre of My World is unapologetically basic; yet undeniable deep.</span>
  <a data-text-id="474724673361776503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2513267905" />
    <a title="Kerry Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/76348176-kerry-patrick"><img alt="Kerry Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515686325p2/76348176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2513267905?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kerry Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kerry Patrick" href="/user/show/76348176-kerry-patrick">Kerry Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307482716" href="/book/show/7001926-the-center-of-the-world">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2513267905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4386472563096214955">in a rare move, i picked this up after i'd seen the movie, which i'd enjoyed. i liked how well the movie seemed to match the story at some points, and how much more there was still left to discover in the book. it took some time to get used to how phil sees his world and talks about it; there was a lot to take in over the years, and i'm afraid i forgot most of his childhood as time jumped back and forth. but i appreciated how much was called back by the end, and how much wasn't. overall it felt </span>
  <span id="freeText4386472563096214955" style="display:none">in a rare move, i picked this up after i'd seen the movie, which i'd enjoyed. i liked how well the movie seemed to match the story at some points, and how much more there was still left to discover in the book. it took some time to get used to how phil sees his world and talks about it; there was a lot to take in over the years, and i'm afraid i forgot most of his childhood as time jumped back and forth. but i appreciated how much was called back by the end, and how much wasn't. overall it felt like there was purpose in all of the vignettes, whether they were for the plot or to just show how phil understood the world and what parts of it went unchallenged. and i liked that his childhood was explored, rather than the life-changing trip he embarks on at the end. at that point his life has already changed, and we've come to learn why it had to. it was refreshing to watch someone run for so long and then leap, while also knowing that whatever comes after that leap doesn't matter.<br /><br />for its rather intricate narrative style, the voice, the phil that i pictured even though i had seen the movie, was even younger. i guess youth is sometimes depicted with simplicity, but i loved that it was more an unrestrained generosity about everything that phil encountered. everything felt important, and as a child, everything is.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4386472563096214955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6336289221905867151">I would have never thought I would ever finish this book, read the last 150 pages in the middle of the night even though I should be asleep by now, when I picked it up randomly from the not as much furnished library of my school. Reading this in German (not my mother tongue) was hard, but I don't know if I would have appreciated it as much in my own language or in English. The beginning was slow, too slow. Then I just got too caught up in the labyrinth of Visible, I guess. And as a fresh 18 year</span>
  <span id="freeText6336289221905867151" style="display:none">I would have never thought I would ever finish this book, read the last 150 pages in the middle of the night even though I should be asleep by now, when I picked it up randomly from the not as much furnished library of my school. Reading this in German (not my mother tongue) was hard, but I don't know if I would have appreciated it as much in my own language or in English. The beginning was slow, too slow. Then I just got too caught up in the labyrinth of Visible, I guess. And as a fresh 18 years old, more or less the same age as Phil, it teached me lessons and gave me answers I didn't think I would find. I didn't feel so caught up in a book for so long! Nor did I feel so inspired by something like this in a while.<br />Especially the ending spoke so much to me, who as Phil feels the need to watch her own world from afar, to grasp it a little more, in my own quest.<br />It shook me from the apathy I fell in during these days and that is what a good book is supposed to do.<br />Every character was built in such a good way, it felt like I actually knew them. The weirdness that surrounds the whole book made it feel so realistic, ironically. <br />It made me feel less alone, understood and comforted, in a way.</span>

<div id="review_492308863" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/492308863" />
    <a title="Carlos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3941555-carlos"><img alt="Carlos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371103576p2/3941555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/492308863?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carlos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carlos" href="/user/show/3941555-carlos">Carlos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780385729437" href="/book/show/1610138.The_Center_of_the_World">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3941555-carlos?shelf=lgbt-sexuality">lgbt-sexuality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3941555-carlos?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer492308863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1564457077108813335">I feel bad saying this but the main problem with this book is that it was too long. Steinhöfel gives an interesting story built around the intermingling of the present with and ever-present past. Unfortunately, the longer the novel drags on the more exhausted the reader becomes. I flew past the first 200 pages but then had to crawl to the finish. It is perhaps telling that my critique is the novel’s length rather than anything else, given that Steinhöfel avoids clichés and manages to find nuance</span>
  <span id="freeText1564457077108813335" style="display:none">I feel bad saying this but the main problem with this book is that it was too long. Steinhöfel gives an interesting story built around the intermingling of the present with and ever-present past. Unfortunately, the longer the novel drags on the more exhausted the reader becomes. I flew past the first 200 pages but then had to crawl to the finish. It is perhaps telling that my critique is the novel’s length rather than anything else, given that Steinhöfel avoids clichés and manages to find nuanced ways to introduce characters, developments and motives. Again, all this suffers from the sheer volume of the story where complete characters, however amusing they seemed, could have been edited out without affecting the novel. Despite its flaws though, Steinhöfel give us a young adult novel that manages to continue where most leave off and show that life does not end with getting the man of our dreams and that it indeed goes forward after he breaks our heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1564457077108813335" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60767008-benjamin?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/60767008-benjamin?shelf=hysterical-bottoms">hysterical-bottoms</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2038856180" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18253046240460621059"><i>Die Mitte der Welt</i> is the story of a boy who grows up gay with his eccentric American mother and timid sister in a small judgemental German town. During the novel, the main character Phil tries to understand the suddenly hostile relationship between his sister and mother, while he gets involved in a secret affair with the reserved Nicholas. Meanwhile, he becomes the victim of an overwhelming jealousy from his best friend Katja's ex-boyfriend, who suspects him of having an affair with Katja.<br/><br/>The n</span>
  <span id="freeText18253046240460621059" style="display:none"><i>Die Mitte der Welt</i> is the story of a boy who grows up gay with his eccentric American mother and timid sister in a small judgemental German town. During the novel, the main character Phil tries to understand the suddenly hostile relationship between his sister and mother, while he gets involved in a secret affair with the reserved Nicholas. Meanwhile, he becomes the victim of an overwhelming jealousy from his best friend Katja's ex-boyfriend, who suspects him of having an affair with Katja.<br /><br />The novel is filled with flashbacks and reflections, which mainly deal with Phil's mother's many lovers, his upbringing without a father, as well as violence and sexual abuse. </span>
  <a data-text-id="18253046240460621059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('76+/tcKMoRX24s/6un7fFUELAgDOJId4pLS80XzF0e+QTJbUIGUDZ4vYblDt5Bo5WPrhqsZ387PT5xPPMwnK8Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('PtpiyBC06Ume+2hQxQcseI2Ha8VlwC6rxrv7BribSMlBOUup8l1LO+PByfqSnelUlHaIb22TWmCx6FQY91dT1w==')})

Bei genau<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText2412982273937357543\" style=\"display:none\">Die in Bayern geborene Hamburgerin Noah Sow hat die Nase voll von den alltäglichen Rassismen, mit denen sie sich als Schwarze permanent konfrontiert sieht. Vieles von dem, was die Autorin beklagt, mag, für sich genommen, harmlos erscheinen. Bei genauer Betrachtung und erst recht in der Summe, sind die vielen kleinen, oft unbewusst stigmatisierenden Etikettierungen für alles, was nicht der offenbar vorherrschenden Vorstellung von dem entspricht, was man als „deutsch“ empfindet, aber tatsächlich eine Zumutung. Das fängt schon damit an, dass man jemanden als „farbig“ bezeichnet, geradeso als sei &quot;weiß quasi der ,Normalzustand\', die ,Ausgangsposition\', und als sei ein ,Farbiger\' sowas wie ein ,angemalter\' oder ,eingefärbter\' Weißer&quot;. Und wer sich bewusst macht, dass der Ausdruck „Mulatte“ dem spanischen &quot;Mulo&quot; (der Mischung aus Esel und Pferd -- zu deutsch: Maultier) entlehnt ist, wird diesen Ausdruck wohl besser aus seinem Wortschatz streichen. Überhaupt: Sprachliche Ungenauigkeiten wie diese, zeigt sich Sow mit guten Gründen überzeugt, helfen mit, „den rassistischen Status quo zu erhalten“. Um den Rassismus zu überwinden müsse man ihn deshalb auch beim Namen nennen und etwa auch rassistische Straftaten als ebensolche bezeichnen -- und nicht als &quot;ausländerfeindlich&quot;, &quot;fremdenfeindlich&quot; oder &quot;rechtsradikal&quot;. Anhand zahlreicher Beispiele zeigt Sow, wie hartnäckig sich koloniale Vorurteile gegenüber Schwarzen halten. Quer durch sämtliche Medien steht das Schwarze -- und sei es &quot;nur&quot; im Subtext -- immer wieder für &quot;brutal, böse, dämonisch&quot;, das Weiße aber für &quot;harmlos, gut, moralisch&quot;. Doch nicht nur solche Etikettierungen prangert Sow an -- auch gut gemeinte Kampagnen, die Schwarzen per se Hilfsbedürftigkeit unterstellen, offenbaren bei genauer Betrachtung einen unbewussten Rassismus und belegen, wie tief das Ressentiment tatsächlich verwurzelt ist. Wer seinen Blick durch die Lektüre dieser Bestandsaufnahme geschult hat, der wird mit Schrecken erkennen, dass die wütende Klage, die die Autorin führt, nur zu berechtigt ist. Unbedingt lesenswert! -- Andreas Vierecke, Literaturanzeiger.de<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"2412982273937357543\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return false;\">...more<\/a>\n\n       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/655104.Andreas_Steinh_fel">About Andreas Steinhöfel</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/655104.Andreas_Steinh_fel"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1369471604p3/655104.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/655104.Andreas_Steinh_fel">Andreas Steinhöfel
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
133
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5642173058287062388">Born in 1962 in Battenberg, Germany, Steinhöfel now works as a translator and reviewer and writes screenplays. First and foremost, though, he is the other of numerous children's and young adult books awarded with various literature prizes. His bestseller "The Center of the World" had been nominated for the well-known and prestigious Germand Youth Literature Prize and has been published in numerous</span>
  <span id="freeText5642173058287062388" style="display:none">Born in 1962 in Battenberg, Germany, Steinhöfel now works as a translator and reviewer and writes screenplays. First and foremost, though, he is the other of numerous children's and young adult books awarded with various literature prizes. His bestseller "The Center of the World" had been nominated for the well-known and prestigious Germand Youth Literature Prize and has been published in numerous countries worldwide.<br /><br />Steinhöfel has been awarded the Erich Kästner Prize in 2009, after Peter Rühmkorf, Loriot, Robert Gernhardt, and Tomi Ungerer. In the same year, he has also been awarded several literature prizes for his works "Rico, Oskar und die Tieferschatten", including the German Youth Literature Prize, the Catholic Childrens' and Youth Literature Prize as well as the "Lesekünstler 2009" award by the Börsenverein Deutscher Buchhandel.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5642173058287062388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
